And the author of this book, upon completing for you, my children, this book which is a part of the science of medicine in its entirety and reaching the pinnacle of clarity and exposition in it, saw fit to complete it for you with this article which is a part of practical work by hand.
For practical work by hand is improved in our country and in our time completely lacking, to the point that its science is almost studied and its trace is interrupted. And what remains of it are slight illustrations in the books of the predecessors, which have been corrupted by hands and subject to error and confusion, until its meanings have become obscure and its benefits distant.
So I saw fit to revive it and compose this article in the manner of explanation, exposition, and summarization, and to provide illustrations of cautery blades and all other surgical instruments, as this is an addition to the clarity and essential for what is needed.
The reason there is no skilled craftsman in our time is because the practice of medicine is long, and its practitioner should first train in the science of anatomy, which Galen described. Until one becomes knowledgeable about the benefits of the organs, their forms, their temperaments, their connections and disconnections, the knowledge of bones, nerves, muscles, their numbers, their origins, and the positions of the outlets of arteries and veins.
For this reason, Hippocrates said that there are many physicians in name but few in deed, especially in the art of the hand. We have mentioned a part of this in the introduction of this book.
For whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have mentioned regarding anatomy is likely to make a mistake that could kill people, as I have witnessed many who have presumed in this science and claimed knowledge without actual learning or understanding.
That is what I saw a ignorant doctor do, who cut into a goiter on the neck of a woman, and thus opened some arteries of the neck causing the woman's blood to flow until she fell dead before him.
And I saw another doctor who proceeded to remove a stone from an old man, and since the stone was large, he took a risk and removed it along with a piece of the bladder. The man died around three days later, and I had been called to remove it, but upon seeing the condition of the stone and the patient, I determined that it was beyond my capability.
And I saw another doctor who was employed by some of the officials in our city to practice medicine.
A young black boy had a fracture in his leg near the ankle with a wound, and the ignorant doctor quickly bound the fracture tightly over the wound with bandages and splints without leaving any room for the wound to breathe.
Then he let him follow his desires, left him for days, and ordered him not to loosen the bindings until his leg and foot swelled, and he was on the brink of death.
I was called to him, so I quickly loosened the bindings, and he gained some relief from his pains. However, the corruption had already taken hold in the limb, and I could not reverse it.
The corruption continued to spread in the limb until he perished.
And I saw another doctor who cut into a cancerous tumor, which ulcerated after days until the sufferer's condition greatly worsened. This is because if the cancer is purely of a dark mixture, it should not be treated with surgery at all.
Unless it is in a limb that can tolerate its complete removal.
And for this, my son, you should know that work with the hand is divided into two parts: work accompanied by safety and work that results in damage in most cases.
And I have warned in every place in this book about the work that involves risk and fear; you should beware of it and reject it.
So that the ignorant do not find a way to criticize or slander, take for yourselves firmness and caution, and for your patients, kindness and thoroughness.
And use the best method leading to safety and praised outcomes, and avoid dangerous and difficult-to-cure diseases.
And keep yourselves from what you fear may bring doubt into your religion and worldly affairs, for it is more lasting for your honor and exalted in this world and the next for your stations.
For Galen said in one of his admonishments: Do not treat bad diseases and thus become bad physicians.
And I have divided this article into three chapters.
The first chapter.
On cauterization with fire and cauterization with sharp medicine, organized and arranged from head to foot, including images of the instruments and cauterizing blades, and everything needed for work by hand.
And the second chapter.
On incisions, bloodletting, cupping, surgery, extraction of arrows, and the like, organized and arranged with images of the instruments.
The third chapter.
On bonesetting, dislocations, and the treatment of swelling and the like, arranged and titled from the head to the foot, with illustrations of instruments.
The first chapter.
On cauterization.
And before we mention working with it, it is advisable to mention the manner of its benefits and drawbacks and in what temperament it is used.
I say that the discussion on the manner of the benefits and drawbacks of cauterization is a long discourse, a precise science, and a hidden secret, and many wise people have spoken about it.
They differed on this, and I have summarized briefly from their discourse to avoid lengthiness.
I say that cauterization generally benefits all sorts of ill temperament, whether with or without matter, except for two temperaments: the hot temperament without matter and the dry temperament without matter.
As for the dry temperament with matter, there is disagreement. Some say that cauterization is beneficial in this case, while others argue the opposite, stating that cauterization is not suitable for a disease caused by heat and dryness because the nature of fire is heat and dryness.
It is impossible to cure a disease that is hot and dry with a treatment that is also hot and dry. Those who argue the opposite claim that cauterization with fire can be beneficial for a hot and dry disease that occurs in people's bodies. For when you add the body of the human and its moisture to the temperament of fire, you affect the body of the human with cold.
And I say by his saying because experience has revealed that to me many times, but this matter should not be imagined except by one who has trained and practiced in the art of cauterization to a high degree. And he noted the differences in people's temperaments and the state of diseases in themselves, their causes, their symptoms, and the duration of time they last.
And as for the other temperaments, there is no need for you to fear them, especially the cold and moist diseases, as all physicians agree on them and do not differ about the benefit of cauterization in them.
And know, O my sons, that one of the secrets of treatment is cauterization with fire and its advantage over cauterization with burning medication because fire is a single essence whose effect does not extend beyond the organ which was cauterized and does not harm another connected organ except with minimal damage.
And cauterization with burning medication may extend its effect to other organs and may cause a disease in the organ that is difficult to treat and may even kill. But fire, due to its nobility and the generosity of its essence, does not do that unless it is excessive.
And this has become clear to us through experience due to the length of service, attention to the craft, and understanding the realities of the matter.
And for this reason, I have dispensed with lengthy discourse, but if it were not inappropriate for my book, I would present to you a mysterious secret about fire and its manner of action on bodies and its removal of diseases with philosophical, demonstrative speech that penetrates your understanding.
And know, O sons, that they have differed about the time in which cauterization is appropriate, and they made the best time the season of spring.
And I say that cauterization may be appropriate at all times, for the harm caused by the time is overshadowed by the benefit brought about by cauterization. Especially if the cauterization is for severe necessary pains that are dangerous and cannot tolerate delay, due to the fear that it might result in a calamity that is greater than the slight harm caused by the time.
Do not let what the common people and ignorant physicians imagine come to your minds, O sons, that cauterization which cures a certain disease will never return, and they consider it permanent.
It is not as they imagine, for cauterization is like medicine that alters the temperament and dries the humidities which are the cause of pains.
However, cauterization is preferred over medicine due to its swift success, strong effect, and severe power.
The disease may return at some time depending on the temperament of the patient, the establishment and strength of his disease, and what accumulates in his body from excesses and neglecting himself in acquiring them from foods and other such causes.
Except if the disease for which cauterization is used is a mild disease in an organ with little excess and humidity. Like cauterizing a tooth for pain and the like, it is possible that such pain may not return, and this occurs rarely.
And as for the common people's saying that cauterization is the end of medicine, it is a correct statement not in line with what they mean, because they believe that no treatment with medication or otherwise is beneficial after cauterization, and the matter is contrary to that.
The meaning of "cauterization is the end of medicine" is that when we use various treatments for a disease and those medicines are ineffective, then we use cauterization as the last resort, which proves effective. From this comes the saying that "cauterization is the end of medicine. Not in the sense that the common people and many ignorant doctors have understood it.
The early scholars mentioned that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron. They said this because gold is balanced and of noble essence, and they claimed that the site of cauterization does not suppurate. However, this is not always the case.
For I have tried it and found that it only does so in some bodies and not others, and cauterization with gold is indeed better and more preferable than with iron as they said. However, when you heat the cautery in the fire, it is not clear to you when it has reached the desired temperature due to the redness of the gold.
Because it quickly cools down, and if you increase the heat, it melts in the fire and becomes liquefied, causing the practitioner to face difficulties. Therefore, cauterization with iron is faster and more accurate for practical purposes, God willing.
I have arranged this chapter on cauterization into sections organized from head to foot to make it easier for the student to find what they need, God willing.
The first chapter.
There is one fontanel in the head.
This fontanel is beneficial for excess moisture and cold affecting the brain, which are causes of headache, frequent discharge from the head to the area of the eyes and ears, excessive sleep, toothache, and throat pain. And in general, for every disease that occurs due to cold, such as paralysis, epilepsy, strokes, and other similar diseases.
The method of this treatment is to order the patient first to purge with a mild, brain-cleansing medicine for three or four nights, according to what is required by the strength of the patient, his age, and his constitution.
Then order him to shave his head with a razor, then seat him in front of you, sitting cross-legged with his hands on his chest.
Then place the base of your palm on the base of his nose between his eyes, and where your middle finger ends, mark that spot with ink.
Then heat the olive-shaped cautery, which looks like this.
Remove enough bone to the size of a clove or a grain of coriander, then lift your hand. If not, repeat with the same iron or another if it has cooled. Until you see the bone as I have described, then take some salt, dissolve it in water, soak a piece of cotton in it, and place it on the area. Leave it for three days.
Then apply cotton soaked in fat on it and leave it until the redness from the inflammation subsides, then treat it with the four-part ointment until it heals, if God wills.
And they say that the wound is better and more beneficial as long as it remains open to discharge pus.
And some mentioned that the skin should be cauterized down to the bone, and the cautery iron should be held until part of the thickness of the bone is burned. Then what has been burned from the bone should be removed and treated thereafter.
And others said that the cauterization should be intensified until it strongly affects the bone, causing a piece to fall off like the shape of a dirham or a small coin. They claimed that this releases vapors from the head and leaves the wound open for a long time.
Then it is treated until it heals. I do not see these types of cauterization at all except in some people and as a risky method, and leaving them is better for safety's sake. For the head weakens whenever its natural connection is dispersed, as we have observed in other organs.
Especially if the patient's head is naturally weak. The first type of cauterization is safer and better in my opinion, and it is what I use. Follow it for safety, if God wills.
The Second Chapter.
On cauterizing the head as well.
If a chronic pain occurs in the head and persists for a long time with the patient, and treatments such as bloodletting, purgatives, cupping, ointments, and dressings have been used, especially if single cauterization which we described has been applied and nothing was beneficial, then consider. If the patient's head is naturally strong in constitution and not weak, and if he feels intense cold, apply another cauterization slightly above the previous one. Then cauterize each horn of his head until the thickness of the skin is reduced and the amount described is exposed from the bone. Cauterize at the back of his head in the area known as the axe, and be gentle with your hand in this case; do not expose the bone because the patient will feel intense pain, more so than from any other cauterization on the entire head. I will mention this cauterization in its proper place.
The cautery used for the horns of the head and its back should be milder than the cautery used for the center of the head, and this is its form.
Chapter Three.
On the cauterization of non-chronic migraines.
If pain accompanied by headache occurs on one side of the head and extends to the eye, make the patient vomit with medicines that cleanse the head and use all other treatments I mentioned in the classifications of diseases. If this does not work, then cauterization should be applied in two ways. Either cauterize with a sharp, burning medicine or with iron.
As for cauterization with a burning medicine, take one clove of garlic, peel it, and cut off the tips from both ends. Then incise the area of pain on the temple with a broad lancet until there is a space under the skin large enough to hold the garlic clove.
It enters under the skin until it disappears, then pull it tightly with a good tightness and leave it for fifteen hours, then release it and remove the garlic and leave the wound for two or three days, then heal.
It is covered with cotton soaked in lard until the area pusces, then treat it with ointment until it heals if God wills. And if you want, you can do that with some of the cauterizing medicines I provided in the eighteenth article on cauterizing medicines.
And as for cauterizing with iron, it is done in this manner: heat the cautery tool which has this shape:.
It is called the nail-shaped cautery because its head is like the shape of a nail, with some perforations, and in the middle, there is a small突起。请注意，最后部分“nub"或"projection"的翻译“突起”在医学历史文本中可能需要更精确的术语，但是根据指示，这里不添加任何解释或注释。因此，“突起”作为对“small nub/projection”的直接翻译被使用了。由于用户要求严格遵循指示且不能包含额外说明，以上微小调整旨在保持句子的流畅性，同时忠实于原文的意思。但如果严格按照要求，正确翻译应为：“It is called the nail-shaped cautery because its head is like the shape of a nail, with some perforations, and in the middle, there is a small projection.”
Then place it on the site of pain and hold your hand as you rotate the iron slightly, and the amount by which you cauterize should be about half the thickness of the skin. Raise your hand so as not to burn the artery below, which could cause bleeding. Then soak some cotton in salt water and place it on the area and leave it for three days. Then soak the cotton in lard, and then treat it with ointment until it heals if God wills.
And if you wish, you cauterize this temple with the knife-like protruding part of the cautery tool, and be careful not to cut the artery in this non-chronic temple especially.
Chapter Four.
Cauterizing the chronic temple.
If you treat the temple with the previously mentioned treatments and what we discussed in the divisions of diseases, and the treatment is not effective, and you see in the condition what cannot be managed by the initial cauterization with medicine or fire that we mentioned. You should heat the knife-like cautery until it turns white, then apply it to the site of pain in a line about half a finger long or so, and leave it once while you hold it tightly until it cuts the artery and reaches near the bone.
However, you should be careful not to affect the jaw that moves during chewing, for if you burn the muscle or nerve that moves it, spasms may occur.
Be cautious and watchful of the bleeding from the artery you have cut, for there is great danger in cutting it. Especially for those who do not know what they are doing and have not tried a proven method, it is better to refrain from the procedure.
The management of accidental bleeding from the artery will be discussed in detail in its appropriate place in the book, God willing. If you see in the condition that this cauterization is not sufficient.
I have seen the body of the patient enduring cauterization in the middle of the head as described, and treat the wound until it heals, if God wills.
And if you wish, use the cautery we mentioned in the chapter on arterial forceps with the two-bladed iron, for it is a better and more effective cautery than this one.
Chapter Five.
On cauterizing the pains of the ears.
If pain occurs in the ear due to cold and is treated with laxatives and other treatments we mentioned in the classification, but the pain does not go away, then heat the cautery known as the point, which has this shape.
Then apply it around the entire ear after heating it, circling around it, or around both ears if the pain is in both. And keep the cautery a little away from the base of the ear after marking the spot with ink. The cautery should be about ten points in each ear or so. Then treat the areas until they heal, if God wills.
Chapter Six.
On cauterizing hemorrhoids.
Hemorrhoids that are treated with cautery are of the type that occur due to phlegm, as I mentioned in the classifications of diseases.
Cauterization should be avoided for the type that occurs due to dryness and nervous spasms.
When you have treated this type of hemorrhoid with suppositories, fumigations, and gargles but your treatment has not been effective, it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cautery sessions. One at the base of the ear, the second slightly below his temple, and the third at the junction of the lips.
Make your cautery on the opposite side of the affected area because the relaxation occurs in the side that appears healthy.
The image of the cautery is to cauterize it opposite the upper part of the ear, slightly below the temple, and another one in the cheek, and its length should be equal to the length of the thumb.
Lower your cautery until it burns to about half the thickness of the skin, and this is the image of the cauterizing tool, which is a type of knife that has been shown before, but it is slightly finer as you can see. It is advisable that the knife should be slightly thicker, then treat the area as previously mentioned until it heals, if God wills.
Chapter Seven.
On the cautery of chronic stroke.
If the stroke becomes chronic and treating it with what we mentioned does not work and there is no fever in the patient, cauterize it with four cauteries. One cautery on each temple of his head, one in the center of the head as we mentioned, and one at the back of the head as previously described.
The description of the cautery is as previously described, and it may also be cauterized at the mouth of the stomach for better effect, then treat it as previously mentioned.
Chapter Eight.
In terms of forgetting.
That which is caused by phlegm should first be treated by giving the patient large decoctions and purified brain cleansers.
Then shave his whole head and apply a mustard poultice, as written in the section on poultices, apply it several times, for it is a form of cauterization.
Do this in the same order I mentioned there, for he will be cured by it. If not, cauterize him three times at the back of his head, arranged from the top of the head to the bottom of the neck.
Make the space between each cauterization the width of a finger, then treat the cauterization as previously described. If you want to increase the treatment and the patient can tolerate it, cauterize the middle area again.
If you wish to increase the treatment, cauterize him on the temples, then continue treating him until he is healed. The cautery should be olive-shaped as previously described.
Chapter Nine.
On the cauterization of hemiplegia and the relaxation of the entire body.
It is necessary to proceed with purifying the head with decoctions as we have mentioned. Then shave the patient's head and cauterize it with one cautery in the middle of the head, one on each temple, and one at the back.
And three on the vertebrae of the neck. If you need more than that for a case of bodily laxity, and if the patient can withstand it and the disease is strong and established, then apply four cauterizations on the vertebrae of his back. And continue with the cauterization until you burn most of the skin, then raise your hand. Then treat it as previously mentioned until it heals, if God wills, and the cautery iron should be olive-shaped.
The Tenth Chapter.
On the cauterization of epilepsy.
Only the epileptic who has epilepsy due to phlegm should be cauterized. It is appropriate to first cleanse his brain with large cathartics and all other treatments we mentioned in the classification, if the patient is an adult and can tolerate taking medications.
As for a child who cannot tolerate medications, use gargles and cleansing mouth rinses to cleanse the brain well in advance, over many days, along with improving his diet.
Then shave his head, then cauterize once in the center of the head as previously described, and another cauterization at the back. And on each temple of his head, apply one cauterization. If the patient is strong and can tolerate it, then apply the cauterizations mentioned for paralysis and bodily laxity on the vertebrae of the neck and back. The cautery iron should be olive-shaped as previously described.
If the patient is a child, make the cautery iron gentle in this manner.
Chapter Eleven.
On the Treatment of Melancholy.
If the cause of melancholy is corrupted humors and thick phlegm, apply the cauterizations we mentioned in the treatment of paralysis.
If the cause of melancholy is an excess inclined towards blackness and the body of the patient is moist, give him what purifies his brain as was mentioned previously in the division.
Then shave the head of the patient. Then make a firm cake from linen in the shape of a circle, then place it in the center of his head while the patient is sitting cross-legged, holding it on all sides. Then take one pound of old sheep's fat.
Then heat it over fire to a moderate warmth, as much as a finger can tolerate when inserted into it. Then pour it in the center of his head within the circle and leave it until it cools. Do this once a week for the patient along with other proper treatments until he recovers, if God wills.
And if you wish, use small scattered cauterizations without holding the cautery iron firmly, but rather by hovering it. For this type of cauterization moistens the brain moderately.
Then apply cotton soaked in sheep's fat or chicken fat to him.
Chapter Twelve.
On the Cauterization for Water Discharge in the Eye.
If it becomes clear to you the beginning of the water flowing into the eye by the signs which were mentioned in the division, then hurry and cleanse the patient’s head and protect it from all moistures and sweat him in the bath on an empty stomach for days.
Then order him to shave his head and cauterize it in the middle of the head, then cauterize two more times on the temples if the water starts flowing into both eyes or from one side if it is in one eye.
Then cut with the cautery all the veins and arteries under the skin, and let the cauterizations be long in the width of the temples, and be cautious of bleeding.
If you see anything of it, then cut it immediately with whatever treatment is possible for you, and we will come to the wisdom in dissecting the arteries, cutting them, and being cautious of bleeding.
It may also be cauterized at the back of the head under the two bones with two significant cautery points.
Chapter Thirteen.
On the cauterization of chronic tears.
If the tears of the eye are chronic and persistent, and they originate from the veins and arteries that are on the outer surface of the head outside the skull, and you are certain that this is due to excessive cold and thick phlegm, then cauterize with the same cautery I described at the beginning of the flowing water. Cauterize in the middle of the head, two cautery points on the temples, and two more at the back of the head under the two bones. If additional treatment is needed, cauterize one point on each side at the corner of the eye near the eyebrow with a small cautery iron.
Chapter Fourteen.
On cauterizing the nose.
If you treat it with what we mentioned in the division and the treatment is not effective, then quickly wash the patient with decoction of colocasia for three nights, then shave his head and cauterize it with a moderate cautery using an olive-shaped cautery iron. Then cauterize slightly above the eyebrows under the hair with a nail-shaped cautery iron twice, and be careful not to cut the artery. This is the image of the nail-shaped iron.
Chapter Fifteen.
On cauterizing the relaxation of the eyelid.
If the eyelid relaxes due to illness or moisture, cauterize the eyelid once with this crescent-shaped cautery iron.
If you wish, cauterize slightly above the eyebrows twice on each side, keeping away from the temples, and the length of each cautery should be equal to the length of the eyebrow.
Do not excess with the cautery; rather, to the degree that a third of the skin is charred, and the shape of the cautery iron should be as described.
Chapter Sixteen.
On cauterizing the eyelid.
If the eyelashes turn inward and irritate the eye, then the cautery for this has two types. Either cauterization with fire or cauterization with a burning medicine. For cauterization with fire, you should have the patient stop plucking his eyelashes, if he does so, until they grow long and even.
For if you graft them when they grow, then bind his eyes with a bandage so that they do not move until they grow. Once they have grown and stabilized, place the patient's head in your lap, then mark on the eyelid with ink in the shape of an oak leaf.
And the beginning of the mark should be near the eyelashes, then place under the eyelid cotton soaked in egg white or in the saliva of the bustard, then heat an iron, this is its shape.
Then iron over the shape you marked little by little in many times until the surface of the skin, which is like the shape of an oak leaf, is burned entirely, especially its outer part. A sign of the success of your work is seeing that the eyelid has tightened and the hair has risen from the eye's flesh.
Then lift your hand at that time and leave it for three days, then apply cotton with fat until the scab falls off, then treat it with ointment until it heals, if God wills. If any hair returns after some time and the eyelid relaxes.
Then repeat the cautery on that area as you did first. If the hair is in the lower eyelid, cauterize it until it returns to its natural position and does not scratch the eye. As for cauterization with a burning agent, it is to have the patient leave the eyelashes until they grow and even out.
Then make a shape of an oak leaf from paper, then take from the known soap and unslaked lime, about one dirham of each. Crush them both very well together, and do this quickly so that they do not dry out. Then spread it on the paper you made like a leaf of as and place it on one or both eyelids and put under the eye cotton soaked in egg white and the patient's head in your lap.
Place your index finger on the medicine and press it slightly while moving it whenever the patient feels the sting of the medicine because he will feel a stinging like fire. As long as he feels the sting, leave the medicine and move it with your finger. When the sting subsides, remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
And observe, if you see the eyelid has risen as it does when cauterized with fire or cut, otherwise, reapply the medicine to the area that was not affected and did not turn black until you complete your work and the eye is cauterized. Then place cotton with fat on it until the inflammation of the burn subsides.
Then treat it with the palm ointment or another until it heals. You should be extremely careful during the procedure to ensure that no part of the medicine falls into the eye, for if the eyelid relaxes after a few days, there is a fear that hair might enter the eye.
Reapply the medicine to the area of the eyelid that has relaxed as you did initially, then treat it until it heals. This is a picture of the leaf of as.
Know that people's eyes may differ in size, so adjust your cauterization accordingly. The right way is not hidden from one who has experience in this craft.
Chapter Seventeen.
On treating the hernia that occurs in the corner of the eye.
If you treat the hernia with what we mentioned in the divisions of diseases and your treatment is not effective, it should be cauterized according to this method.
Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap, and have a servant hold his head between your hands so that he does not move or shake his head.
Then, place cotton soaked in egg white or in the saliva of a catfish on his eyes, then heat the cautery which looks like this.
It should be hollow like the shape of an eagle feather tube on one end where the cautery is, and if you wish, the other end can be open, or it can be closed like a rod, but this hollow one is better for your work, God willing.
Then, squeeze the hernia if it is open and remove the pus, dry it, or if it is not open, then open it and extract its purulent matter. Then place the heated cautery, which is very hot, on it, holding it firmly until it reaches the bone.
Move your hand slightly away from the eye toward the nose during cauterization so that your hand does not make a mistake or startle the patient, causing the cautery to fall into the eyelid and damage it. If you reach the bone on the first attempt, if not, repeat the cautery if necessary.
Leave it for three days, then apply cotton with fat and treat it with a drying ointment until it heals. If forty days pass and it does not heal, apply an abrasive and corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed and scrape it as will be mentioned in its section, God willing.
Another method for cauterizing the hernia mentioned by some early practitioners is to direct attention to the site of the hernia, cut it open, then place a thin tube into the incision, this is its shape.
Pour into it an amount of molten lead weighing a dirham, and hold the tube firmly without movement, and the patient must not move at all so that the molten lead does not flow to his eye, and you should place cotton soaked in egg white or water on the patient's eye.
For the lead burns the site of the hernia and cures it wonderfully. If the hernia is healed by what we have mentioned of cauterization and treatment, then there is no need for further action; otherwise, it is necessary to use nasal piercing and return the hernia to the nasal passage as will be detailed in the specific section on this topic.
Chapter Eighteen.
On cauterizing the cleft lip.
A cleft often occurs in the lip called a slit, especially in the lips of children, as it frequently happens. If you treat this cleft with what we have mentioned in the section on division and the treatment is not effective, then heat a small knife cauterizer shaped like this.
Its hollow should be as thin as a knife, then place it while hot quickly into the cleft until the cauterization reaches the depth of the cleft, then treat it with keroty until it heals, if God wills.
Chapter Nineteen.
On cauterizing the abscess occurring in the mouth.
If a tumor appears at the base of the gums or in the palate or at the roots of the molars, then it becomes hard and bursts, and pus flows out forming an abscess, and if treating it does not succeed, you should heat a cautery to the extent that it can fit into the abscess.
Then, insert it while hot into the abscess hole and hold your hand until the iron reaches deep inside it and its end, do this once or twice, then treat it with what we have mentioned of treatments until it heals, if God wills.
If the material is severed and it heals, well and good; otherwise, it is necessary to examine the area and remove the diseased bone according to what will come in its chapter, if God wills.
Chapter Twenty.
On cauterizing loose teeth and gums.
If the gums become loose due to moisture and the teeth move, and treating them with medicines is ineffective, place the patient's head on your lap, then heat the cautery, which will be depicted after this, after placing the tube on the tooth.
Then insert the heated cautery quickly and hold your hand for a little while until the patient feels the heat has reached the root of the tooth, then raise your hand. Then repeat the cautery several times as desired, then have the patient rinse their mouth with salt water.
Hold it for a while and then remove it, for the loose tooth will become stable, the relaxed gums will tighten, and the harmful moisture will dry up.
Chapter Twenty-One.
On the Pain of the Tooth.
If the toothache is due to cold or there is a worm in it and treatment with medicines is ineffective, then cauterization is done in two ways: either by cauterization with fat or by cauterization with fire.
As for cauterization with fat, it is to take buffalo fat, boil it in an iron spoon or a shell, then take cotton, wrap it around the end of a probe, dip it in the boiled fat, and place it on the painful tooth quickly, holding it until it cools.
Then repeat it several times until the heat reaches the root of the tooth. If you wish, you can dip a wick or cotton in cold fat and place it on the painful tooth, then put a heated iron above it until the heat reaches the bottom of the tooth.
As for cauterization with fire, it is to take a copper or iron tube that has some thickness so that the heat of the fire does not reach the patient's mouth. Then, heat the cautery tool, which is depicted in its form, and place it directly on the tooth, holding your hand until the cautery tool cools. Do this several times.
The pain will disappear either that very day or the next day. After the cauterization, the patient should fill his mouth with good fat, hold it for an hour, then spit it out. This is the form of the cautery tool.
Cauterize with whichever end you prefer and to the extent possible. This is the form of the tube.
Chapter Twenty-Two.
On castrating pigs.
If the pigs suffer from phlegm and cold moistures, and do not mature with medications, and you want quick maturity, heat the hollow iron, which has its ends perforated, as shown in its figure.
So that smoke comes out from the other end when cauterizing, place it heated on the same swelling once and twice if needed until you reach the depth of the swelling. If the swelling is small, make the iron according to the size of the swelling.
Then leave it for three days and apply cotton soaked in fat until what was burned by the fire is gone, then treat it with ointment and lint until it heals, if God wills.
Chapter Twenty-Three.
On cauterization for hoarseness of the voice and shortness of breath.
If moistures overwhelm the windpipe, especially if this is accompanied by a cold temperament, it is appropriate to first purge the patient with laxative medicines, then cauterize him at the indentation of the neck near the base of the throat in the lower area.
Beware that the cauterization does not reach the throat, and do not burn more than half of the skin. Then cauterize another spot at the joint of the neck at the last prominent vertebra, and the cautery iron should be awl-shaped as previously described.
Then treat it with what was previously mentioned until it heals, if God wills.
Chapter Twenty-Four.
On Treating Lung Disease and Cough.
If the cough and lung disease are due to cold moisture and there is no fever or consumption in the patient, and the disease is chronic, cauterize two spots above the clavicles at the low, soft, empty areas and another cauterization in the middle of the chest between the breasts.
The cautery should be needle-shaped as previously described. If you prefer, your cauterization may be done by puncture with the cautery tool called the point, whose image was previously described in the puncturing of ear pain, and the number of points should be around thirty or so.
Then treat it with what was previously mentioned until it heals. You may also make a cautery instrument with three prongs in this shape to expedite the cauterization, as you can perform three cauterizations at once with it. This is the shape of the cautery instrument.
Chapter Twenty-Five.
On Cauterizing the Armpit.
If the head of the humerus dislocates due to slippery moisture or does not stay in place when reduced, so that it becomes habitual and dislocates at the slightest movement as we have observed, it should first be reduced. Then the patient should lie on their back or on the correct side. Then raise the skin inside the armpit upwards with the fingers of your left hand if the joint has dislocated inward.
Then heat the iron with two blades which looks like this.
Then iron the skin until it penetrates to the other side and the shape of the branding will be four brands, and sometimes it is branded with an iron that has three blades, in which case the shape of the branding will be six brands, and the blades should be as thin as the material allows.
And this is the image of the iron with three blades.
And one may be added to this number so the brands are eight, then attach to the branding finely ground balls with salt, then the patient must rest and not move the limb for a time until it strengthens, and if the dislocation is upward, which seldom occurs.
Brand above the shoulder a single nail-like brand or several punctate brands, for the joint will strengthen, moisture will dissipate, and the patient will heal.
Chapter Twenty-Six.
On branding the stomach.
If cold and excessive moisture occur in the stomach, causing it to deviate from its temperament, and if various treatments have been ineffective, then the patient should lie on his back, extend his legs and arms, and then be branded with three brands. One brand below the nipple, the size of a finger, with a nail-like iron, and two brands below on both sides of the single brand so that the shape of the brands forms a triangle, spaced apart so they do not come together if pus forms, and the depth of the branding should be about two-thirds the thickness of the skin, and this is the shape of the brands.
In this manner and to this extent, no more.
And if you wish, make one large scar in the center of the stomach as follows.
And the cautery with which this single scar is made should be circular, as follows.
And the stomach may be cauterized by spots for those who are apprehensive of this cautery. This is done by marking points on the stomach with ink to the extent you desire, then cauterizing them with a spotted cautery, and then treating it with the previously mentioned treatment until it heals.
Chapter Twenty-Seven.
On cauterizing the cold liver.
If pain in the liver is due to cold and moisture or to a foul humor until it has departed excessively from its natural temperament, and if the patient's treatment with what we mentioned in the division does not succeed. It is advisable that the patient lie on their back, and mark three cautery points with ink on the liver, below the ribs where the arm of a person ends, in this shape and exactly this quantity.
There should be the thickness of a finger between each cautery mark. The cautery should be made along the length of the body in a straight line, and do not press your hand tightly on the cautery iron.
The heat should be such that it burns half the thickness of the skin, no more. The patient should stand on their feet; if they cannot stand, they should lie down with their legs extended and arms raised. This is the shape of the cautery iron.
You may apply these cauterizations with a knife-shaped iron if you have the skill and caution to perform it, taking care not to overdo the cautery so as to burn all the skin, thereby burning the abdomen and reaching the intestines, for the skin there is thin, so be aware of this.
Chapter Twenty-Eight.
On cauterizing the swelling of the liver.
If there is an abscess in the liver and you want to determine if that swelling is in the liver's flesh or its membrane, then if it is in the liver's flesh, the patient will feel a heavy pain without sharpness.
If it is in the membrane of the liver, there will be a sharp severe pain. I have observed that its treatment has often exhausted physicians. It should be that the patient lies on their back, then you apply ink to the swollen area for identification.
Then heat the cautery in the fire, which is the cautery that resembles a chisel, and this is its shape. Cauterize it once with it until all the skin is burned, and continue the cautery until you reach the membrane, thus removing all the pus, then treat it as you would an abscess until it heals.
This type of cauterization should only be performed by someone who has extensive experience in the practice of medicine and has dealt with these diseases multiple times through experience. In that case, they may undertake such work, but I consider leaving it to them the best option.
Chapter Twenty-Nine.
On the cauterization of the hemorrhoids.
The early scholars mentioned cauterization with the roots of the zeraund for cold hemorrhoids in this manner: take one long dry root of zeraund, as long as you can find, and it should be as thick as a finger. Then dip it in oil and ignite it in fire. Then cauterize it with one large cautery between the connection of the collarbone and the neck, two small cauterizations slightly below the veins leaning towards the side under the chin, and two large cauterizations above the breasts, between the third and fourth ribs.
Two more cauterizations between the fifth and sixth ribs, slightly tilted backwards. Another cautery in the middle of the chest and another above the stomach. Three cauterizations from behind: one between the shoulders and two beside the spine, below the cautery that is between the palms.
You should not penetrate deeply with the cautery but it should be on the surface of the skin slightly. Some early scholars mentioned that some people used an iron cautery resembling a nail, heating it and inserting it between the ribs until it reaches the tumor itself.
The treatment is expelled as we mentioned in the case of liver tumors. Cauterization in this area is dangerous; either the patient may die immediately, or an incurable fistula may develop in the area.
Chapter Thirty.
On the cauterization of the spleen.
If you treat the spleen disease with the treatments we mentioned in the division and it does not work, then cauterization can be done in three ways, all of which are correct. One of them is to apply three or four cauterizations arranged along the length of the spleen.
In the shape of the liver cauterizations that are presented in its form, and there is between each cauterization the thickness of a finger or slightly more, and the nature of the cautery is what we mentioned for the liver cautery, and do not deepen your hand in the cautery, and the patient's image is lying on his back.
And the other side is in the elbow, and you lift the skin opposite the spleen where the patient's left elbow ends, and lifting the skin should be across the body so that the cauterizations fall along the length of the body.
Then insert the two very hot probes until they penetrate the skin on the other side, then remove the cautery so that there are four cauterizations. If you wish to use the other cautery with three probes.
Then treat the site of the cautery after allowing it to discharge pus for many days, as this is more effective than all the previous treatments mentioned.
Chapter Thirty-One.
On cauterizing ascites.
Cauterization is only beneficial for dropsical ascites, specifically. If you have treated the person with various treatments mentioned in the classification and your treatment has not been effective, it is advisable to cauterize with four cautery marks around the navel and one on the stomach.
Another cautery on the liver, one on the spleen, two behind his back between the shoulder blades, one opposite his chest, and another opposite his stomach. The depth of the cautery should be close to the thickness of the skin. Then leave the cautery open to discharge pus for a long time.
Do not stop treating the patient after cauterization with what is appropriate, as it combines both meanings and hastens recovery. The shape of the iron used for cauterizing the back should be nail-shaped, as previously described, and that used for the back should be olive-shaped.
Chapter Thirty-Two.
On Cauterizing the Feet and Legs.
If they swell in the edema and are filled with yellow water, it is appropriate to cauterize on the top of the foot between the little toe and the ring toe.
Hold the cauterizing iron with your hand and do not bend it. Then raise your hand and do not return it at all, for the yellow water will drain out. The cauterizing iron should be shaped like this.
Then cauterize both legs, twice on each leg. The cauterization should be done with the blade end of the cautery iron. The cauterizations should be along the length of the leg, one below the knee and another below it towards the middle of the leg. Each thigh should also receive two cauterizations.
Leave the cauterization open without treatment for a long time, allowing the water to drain from it. Then treat it with all the methods we have mentioned.
Chapter Thirty-Three.
On Cauterizing Diarrhea.
If the diarrhea is due to cold and moisture, which weakens the holding and digestive powers in the stomach and intestines, and if it has not healed with various treatments, and you see that the patient can tolerate cauterization and is strong enough, then cauterize them with a large cautery on their stomach. As mentioned previously regarding ironing the stomach with a circular iron and four irons around the navel, use the delicate nail iron lightly, or an iron on cotton over the anus, large or two.
If you see the humidities abundant and the patient tolerating that, then apply an iron on the pubic area, an iron on each side, and sometimes add two small irons on the stomach near the large one. For it is a successful treatment whose benefit does not fail, if God wills.
Chapter Thirty-Four.
On ironing hemorrhoids of the anus.
If there are chronic hemorrhoids, whether many or one, and they are composed of thick cold mixtures or corrupt humidities, and have been treated with what we mentioned in the division but the treatment was ineffective, then apply three irons to the patient on the lower part of the sacral vertebrae slightly below the waist in a triangular shape.
An iron below the navel by about two fingers, and if you determine that his stomach has cooled and his food is not digesting and you see his face swollen, then apply a large iron on his stomach as previously mentioned and an iron on his liver. And another on his spleen with a nail iron. Leave the ironing open for a while, then treat him until he recovers, if God wills.
Chapter Thirty-Five.
On ironing warts.
After cutting it, if the polyp is cut, heat the iron which resembles a mill then insert it hot into the center of the cut polyp and push your hand until the iron reaches the source of the bleeding. Do this once or twice.
If the warts are numerous, cauterize each one as described, then treat them with appropriate ointments until they heal. Cauterizing them again over cotton can be more beneficial.
Chapter Thirty-Six.
On cauterizing the hemorrhoid that occurs in the anus and its surrounding areas.
If the patient does not respond to incision and the procedure we described in its place and is afraid of that, it may heal by cauterization. If one develops a hemorrhoid and it persists, with pus and corrupt humors flowing from it, the first thing you should do is measure it with a thin probe.
Then determine its depth with the probe. Then heat the iron which resembles a mill and insert it hot into the hemorrhoid straight to the depth of the probe's entry. Repeat the cauterization until all the corrupt substances are burned, once or twice or three times as needed.
Be careful not to burn a nerve or a major vein, especially if the hemorrhoid leads to the bladder or the intestines.
Be cautious of all these areas. You should only do this if the hemorrhoid is in a fleshy area and you determine that it is not perforated. Then treat the area until it heals. If the area becomes sealed, the secretion stops, and remains so for a period of time, know that it has healed completely.
And if the materials do not cease from him, know that it is penetrable or there is rotten bone in its depth or something like what will be mentioned in its place.
Chapter Thirty-Seven.
On Treating the Kidneys.
If pain occurs in the kidney due to cold or dense wind and the patient's strength decreases because of it, it is advisable to cauterize on both sides directly on the kidney with a nail cauterizer as previously mentioned. Sometimes we might cauterize a third time on the same spot so that there are three cauterizations in a row, which is more effective for treatment.
Chapter Thirty-Eight.
On Cauterizing the Bladder.
If weakness and laxity occur in the bladder due to cold and moisture until the patient cannot hold urine, cauterize once below the navel on the bladder where pubic hair begins, and cauterize once to the right of the navel and another to its left.
The cauterization on each side should be about the width of a thumb joint, and cauterize once at the lower back or twice if necessary. The cauterizer should be nail-shaped as previously mentioned.
Chapter Thirty-Nine.
On Cauterizing the Womb.
If cold and moisture cause a substance to form in the womb, preventing conception and spoiling its function, or if pain occurs upon its arrival, it is advisable to cauterize three times around the navel as mentioned in the cauterization of the bladder. Brand on cotton below the back or two brands and the iron should be spiky.
Chapter Forty.
On how to dislocate the hip.
Erroneous moistures may affect the hip joint, causing it to dislocate. Its sign is that one leg appears longer than the other when comparing them side by side, and you will find an empty space where the dislocation occurred. It should be treated by branding the affected area around the hip joint in a circular shape.
After you mark with ink around the joint as it circles, so that the joint itself is in the center of the circle. The iron used should be as previously described for branding the stomach. If this iron is not available, then use the large olive-shaped iron to brand three times.
Make the brand deep according to the thickness of the entire skin, then treat it until it heals, if God wills.
Chapter Forty-One.
On branding for sciatica.
If pain occurs in the hip joint and the cause is cold and moisture, and if the treatment mentioned in the division has not been effective and the condition has persisted, it should be treated by purging the patient with strong purgatives such as black seed or senna seeds, or similar.
Then brand it, and there are two methods of branding: either branding with burning medicines or branding with fire. Branding with fire can be done in various ways, one of which is to brand three triangular brands on the hip joint itself, like this shape.
And it should have a suitable depth, and there should be between each cauterization and the next the thickness of a finger, and the cautery iron should be olive-shaped. Sometimes a single cauterization is made in the middle on the hipbone itself, thus making four cauterizations. And if you wish, use the circle previously mentioned for dislocating the hip with one cauterization.
To make the circle enclose all of the hip and burn through the entire thickness of the skin, this is the description of the cautery for sciatica if the pain is confined to the hip itself and does not extend to the thigh and leg.
If it extends to the thigh and leg, then apply two cauterizations on the thigh at the place where the patient indicates the pain is felt, and one above the ankle by four fingers slightly towards the outer side. The cautery iron should be knife-shaped, and the depth of the cauterization should be only as thick as the skin.
And if he indicates that the pain extends towards the toes, cauterize where he points with a point cautery three or four times, or more if necessary. If he indicates the pain is below the knee towards the leg, cauterize there once with a knife-shaped cautery iron.
And be careful in all your cauterizations that you do not go so deep as to burn a nerve or a major artery, thereby causing the patient a severe or permanent disability.
I have seen cases where cautery was performed above the ankle and was excessive, causing gangrene in the leg until it reached the foot, perforating it entirely and ruining the entire limb, then diarrhea occurred followed by death. If the pain is on both sides, cauterize them both in the same manner described.
Some of the wise scholars have mentioned in cauterizing the hip, its description is as follows: a vessel-like object is made from iron and its diameter is half a shibr. Its mouth should be as thick as a date stone or slightly less. Inside this vessel there are another two vessels.
And there should be the width of a thumb joint between each vessel. The vessels are open on both sides, and their height is about one or two joints. A handle made of iron, firmly attached to the vessels, is created for them, and this is its form.
Then it is heated in the fire until it turns red and spits sparks. Then it is placed on the affected hip, with the patient lying on the healthy side, and it cauterizes it with three circular cauterizations at once. Then it leaves it for three days and dresses it with fat, leaving the wound open for some days.
Then treat it with ointment until it heals. The author of this book says that this type of cauterization is rarely used due to its unpleasantness and the horror of its appearance, and few are those who can endure it. However, it is an effective cauterization for those who can withstand it and apply it correctly.
As for cauterization with burning medications, it involves making two vessels like rings into which the lead of the pipe can be placed, made of brass or iron.
There should be a height of about two joints or so around them, and the distance between them should be the thickness of a finger. They should be open at both the bottom and the top, and they should be joined together in this manner.
Then place it on the true hip with the patient lying on his sound side, and firmly hold your hand. Then pour between the two circles some sharp water that has been warmed by fire a little, and keep it for about an hour; the patient should endure its stinging and burning, as he will feel a sting like fire.
Until the stinging subsides, then raise your hand with the instrument and wash all the sharp water off the hip with fresh water. Then leave it for three days and apply fat to it until the blackness of the burn disappears. Leave it for some days until pus flows from it, as this is more beneficial.
Then treat it with ointments until it heals. If the pain extends to the thigh or leg, make a poultice for him as something that retains water according to what you did for the hip equally. This is the description of sharp water and I have confirmed it in the article on preparing medicines.
Take an equal amount of soda ash and unslaked lime, crush them, and place them in a new pot that has one small hole at the bottom, just large enough for the liquid to pass through. Place another glass pot under the bottom of the pot.
Pour fresh water over the soda ash and lime, enough to cover them by a finger's depth after you have firmly pressed them with your hand. Leave the pot until the sharp water drips into the lower glass pot. Then collect all of that water and pour it over another portion of lime and soda ash, also renewed.
It is then extremely sharp and can be used in many medical procedures and for cauterizing various body parts, as it acts like fire itself. Some medicines that can also be used to cauterize the hip include colocynth, baladrana honey, lime mixed with soap, all pounded together.
Galen reported a story about an ancient man's treatment for hip pain and sciatica, greatly exaggerating its importance, claiming that it does not need any other treatment and that it cures in one attempt.
To the extent that he might enter the bath carried and come out cured. This is done by taking green mercury, and if green is not available, then fresh dry [mercury] should be taken, ground finely with some fat, and applied to the hip where the pain is, or on the leg, or on the thigh.
It is tied and left for about three hours or until the patient feels that the burning has subsided, then he enters the bath. When his body starts to sweat, he should enter the pool, for the pain will go away and he will be cured by the will of God. If he is not cured, repeat the poultice again after ten days.
For he will be cured if God wills. Know that one should not use cauterization with these medications unless the body has been purged. Dioscorides mentioned that goat dung, if used to cauterize sciatica, is beneficial for it.
The cauterization should be done as follows: take some wool, soak it in old oil, and place it on the deep spot between the thumb and the wrist, which is closer to the wrist. Then, take dry goat dung.
Ignite it with fire until it becomes a coal, then place it on the wool and leave it until it is extinguished. Then take another piece and continue doing this until the sensation reaches the middle of the arm to the hip, and the pain subsides by the will of God. This type of cauterization is called dung cauterization.
Chapter Forty-Two.
On treating back pain.
Pain in the back may arise from various causes, such as a fall, a blow, excessive vomiting, and the like. It results from the accumulation of cold, moist matter, and cauterization is only applicable to this type.
When the pain results from the accumulation of cold matter, after the patient is purged with aromatic seeds and the like, cauterization should be performed on the back where the pain occurs, in three rows across the affected area. The location should first be marked with ink. In each row, there should be five cautery points or more, depending on what you see fit based on the patient's tolerance and strength.
Cauterization should be done with a point cauterizer. If you prefer, you can perform three or four cautery points with a medium-sized double-pronged cauterizer in this manner.
Chapter Fifty-Three.
On cauterizing the initial stages of hunchback.
This condition often affects young children. A sign of its initial onset in a child is difficulty breathing when standing and moving, and you may find a protruding vertebra at the end of their spine that stands out from the other vertebrae.
If you observe this and wish to halt its progression, cauterize it with a circular cautery tool in this manner. Apply the cautery equally on each side of the vertebra. If you prefer, cauterize around the vertebra in two or three rows with a point cauterizer, ensuring the points are close to each other. Then treat the area until it heals as mentioned.
And it is important not to use cauterization on the hump that results from nerve spasm.
Chapter Forty-Four.
On Cauterizing Gout and Joint Pains.
If the joint pains are due to cold humidities that affect any part of the body, and if the pains occur in the legs, it is customary for physicians to call this gout particularly.
If cold gout is treated with the various treatments we mentioned in the classification and the pains do not subside, then cauterization can alleviate them. This involves cauterizing around the joints of the legs after purging, performing many cautery sessions. The cauterizer should be olive-shaped and medium-sized, resembling this form.
And if you need to apply cauterization to the foot's surface, do so with a point cautery. If the pains ascend to the knees or other joints, which often occurs, cauterize each knee with three or four cautery sessions on each side using the same olive-shaped cautery.
If more cauterization is needed, perform it, but do not penetrate deeply with the cautery; it should only be as deep as the thickness of the skin. If the pains ascend to the hips or back, use the cauterization methods we have described for those areas.
If the pains are only in the hands, apply point cautery around the wrists in two rows. If the pain persists in the fingers, apply a point cautery on each joint and on the palm. If the pains ascend to the elbows or shoulders after a few days.
Treat both from all sides and do not let the patient lack good management and taking of medicines, for if he improves his diet and expels phlegm, then he will recover with this cauterization, if God wills.
Chapter Forty-Five.
On cauterizing fistulas.
If a hernia appears in the groin and part of the intestine and scrotum descends into the testicle, and this is newly occurred and recent, it is advisable to order the patient to abstain from food for a day and to use laxatives that will expel stool from his body.
Then he should lie down in front of you on his back, and order him to hold himself until the scrotum or intestine protrudes, then push it back with your finger. Then mark with ink under the hernia on the pubic bone a sign resembling a half-circle, its ends toward the upper body.
Then heat an iron that looks like this.
Until it comes white and throws off sparks, then push the intestine or scrotum back into his body. Then a servant should place his hand on the area to prevent the intestine from protruding. The patient's legs are spread apart, and a pillow is placed under him. Another servant binds his legs.
Another person should be on his chest, holding his hands. Then place the iron directly on the mark and press with the iron standing straight and hold it until it reaches the bone, or repeat once more if it did not reach the bone the first time.
You must protect your effort from the protrusion of the intestine while cauterizing so as not to burn it, which could result in either the death of the patient or a great disability. Know that if you do not reach the bone with the cauterization, your work will not succeed. The cautery for children should be delicate according to their size and for adults according to their size.
Then, treat the cauterized area after three days with fat until the fire's roughness disappears, then continue treating it with ointments until it heals. Let the patient lie on their back for forty days until the wound is completely sealed.
You should make his diet during the treatment period what soothes his stomach so that the intestine does not protrude when defecating. Then, if he wishes to get up after forty days, use a tight bandage and keep it on for another forty days. He should reduce exertion, overeating and drinking, and loud shouting.
For if this procedure is followed, he will be completely healed, God willing. I will discuss the treatment of hernias by incision in its own section, God willing. As for a hernia that occurs elsewhere in the abdomen and is new, if you want to prevent it from worsening, cauterize the area with a round cautery according to its size. Let what you burn of the skin be about two-thirds, then treat it as we have described, for it will not worsen, God willing. Some early practitioners have mentioned cauterizing the hernia with a triangular cautery in this manner.
After you outline the hernia with ink, make a line across at the upper side of the hernia and another line downward. Place your hand in the middle and use one nail-shaped cautery. The first cauterization is easier and better, God willing.
Chapter Forty-Six.
On cauterizing the uterus.
If pain occurs in some organs due to a fall or blow and that pain persists for a long time and treatment with medicines is ineffective, it should be cauterized with a cautery of puncture. The cauterization of each organ should be according to its size, strength, and weakness.
If the pain persists and affects the uterus, and if it heals from the first cauterization, well and good; otherwise, you should repeat the cauterization because such pains usually move from one organ to a nearby one. You should follow it with cauterization until the patient is healed.
Chapter Forty-Seven.
On cauterizing leprosy.
As for lepers, they may greatly benefit from cauterization, especially those with leprosy caused by the corruption of phlegm and black bile.
If you want to cauterize it, examine it. If the leprosy is in its early stages and treatment with what we mentioned in the classification has not been effective and you fear that corruption may take over the entire temperament of the patient, cauterize him on the head with five cautery applications. The first one in the middle of the head, the second below it towards the forehead at the end of the hair, two on the temples, and one from behind on the occipital protuberance. Insert your hand slightly with the cautery so that it affects the bone a little.
And remove the scales from it to facilitate the breathing of the thick vapors and cauterize it like the spleen as mentioned before, and if leprosy has persisted in the patient and appeared clearly, then it should be cauterized with these cauterizations which we mentioned for the head. Cauterize at the tip of the nose, two cauterizations on the cheeks, two on the neck vertebrae, six on the back vertebrae, one large one on the buttocks at the base of the tail, another above it on the same plate, and two on the hips, one on each hip. And two on the knees, one on each knee, two on the shoulders, two on the elbows, two on the ribs of the chest, and cauterize each joint of his fingers and toes with a cauterization, and on each heel of his feet and the wrists of his hands.
And be careful of the nerves at the back of the heels so as not to burn them. It may also be cauterized on the pubic bone, another on the mouth of the stomach, and another on the liver. Know that the more you increase the cauterizations, the more beneficial and effective it is.
And know that the patient does not feel pain from cauterization as a healthy person would, because his body has become numb. The cauterizations should be of varying sizes according to the organs and joints, as previously described for the characteristics of the instruments.
Then treat the cauterization with crushed cress seeds mixed with honey and other treatments until it heals, if God wills.
Chapter Forty-Eight.
In cauterizing numbness, when a body part becomes numb and is treated with medicines, ointments, and dressings but does not heal, then cauterize the numb body part itself according to whether the part is large or small. Let your cauterization be slightly deeper in the thickness of the skin.
Then treat it with ointment until it heals. Cauterization may also be performed for some numbness that affects the hand or foot due to issues in the vertebrae where the nerves that move that body part exit, which can alleviate the numbness.
None but those who are knowledgeable about the anatomy of body parts and the exits of the nerves that move the body should undertake this.
Chapter Forty-Nine.
On Cauterizing Ulcers.
If an ulcer persists and no medical treatment is effective, then cauterize it slightly deep into the thickness of the skin until the whiteness disappears and its color changes.
Then treat it with ground lentils mixed with rose oil, pennyroyal leaves, and pigeon's blood or the blood of doves, using an equal part of each. Mix everything together and apply it to a cloth, which should be kept in place until it heals.
Chapter Fifty.
On Cauterizing Cancer.
If the cancer is in its early stages and you wish to halt its progression, cauterize around it in a circular manner with a circular cautery. Some wise men have suggested making a severe cauterization in its center, but I do not agree with this because I anticipate that it may ulcerate, and I have observed this occurrence multiple times.
The correct thing is to cauterize around it in a circle as we said or with many cautery points.
Chapter Fifty-One.
On cauterizing the hernia.
If a person develops a hernia and it delays in maturing, either due to the influential humor causing it, or due to the age of the patient if he is an elderly person with little blood, or due to time, and you wish to hasten the maturity of the hernia, cauterize around it with many small cautery points drop by drop.
Then leave it, for it will hasten to mature. If you want to cauterize its base, heat the cautery instrument which looks like this.
Place it in the center of the hernia until it penetrates the skin, and let the cauterization be on the lower part to facilitate the flow of pus. Then treat it as appropriate until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-Two.
On cauterizing the cancer.
Cancer is a corruption that spreads in the organ, consuming it like fire consumes dry wood. If you see cancer in a place that can be cauterized with fire, heat many nail-shaped cautery instruments, both small and large, according to what is suitable for the location of the cancer.
Then cauterize it from all sides until all the corruption is completely removed and nothing remains. Then leave it for three days, and apply powdered sulfur with oil to the cauterized areas until all the scabs and corruption fall off entirely.
Then treat it with poultices that promote flesh growth. If you see after three days that the flesh grows properly without corruption, otherwise repeat the cauterization on what remains of the corrupted areas. The ulcer can be treated with sharp medicine.
For it serves as a substitute for fire with quicker efficacy. I have mentioned its treatment with sharp medicine in the division, so take it from there whenever you need it.
Chapter Fifty-Three.
On the cauterization of reversed and non-reversed nails.
This condition often occurs on the soles of the feet, and it is a rough thing that irritates the person. Cauterization for this has two forms: either cauterization with fire or cauterization with sharp water.
As for cauterization with fire, it involves heating a hollow iron instrument similar to an eagle's feather. The instrument should be made of iron and sized to fit around the nail on all sides, with a thin edge. Then place the heated instrument over the nail and rotate your hand around the nail with the instrument until it reaches the depth of the nail.
Leave it for three days until pus forms, then dress it with crushed wild thyme mixed with salt. Leave the dressing on overnight, and the nail will be pulled out from its root. Then treat the wound site with a flesh-growing ointment until it heals. If the nails are not reversed.
This condition often occurs on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and legs. You should take a tube made of copper or iron or shaped like an eagle's feather, place it over the nail or wart, and then pour a small amount of sharp water into the tube.
Hold your hand while turning it with a slight twitch so that the edge of the tube affects the base of the nail, and let the sharp water find its way to penetrate to the base of the nail, and let the patient endure the sting of the sharp water for a moment.
Then leave it, for the nail will be extracted with its root. Do this one by one until you have treated all of them in the body, then treat the areas after extraction with ointments that promote flesh growth.
Chapter Fifty-Four.
On cauterizing the tonsils.
If one of the tonsils is affected by cold in the nerve or by quartan fever or the like, it should be cauterized four or five times between the vertebrae with one cautery per vertebra and once on the chest. And on his stomach, apply one cautery with an olive-shaped cauterizer, for the tonsil will subside and hasten the maturation of the cold disease.
Chapter Fifty-Five.
On cauterizing abscesses that occur in the body.
Sometimes, ugly abscesses may appear in the body due to thick, cold, and corrupted materials. When they first appear, each abscess should be gently cauterized at its head using a heated cautery stick, or the root of a long reed, or a lentil-shaped cauterizer.
Cauterize the blisters when they first appear in this manner; it will prevent their increase, disperse the causative substance, and the patient will recover. However, this should be done after the patient has been purged with a venesection.
Chapter Fifty-Six.
On staunching the bleeding that occurs when an artery is cut.
Bleeding often occurs from a severed artery when a wound is exposed externally or when a tumor is cut open or an organ is cauterized, and the like, making it difficult to sever it.
If this happens to someone, quickly reach with your hand to the mouth of the artery and place your index finger on it and hold it firmly so that the blood is contained under your finger and nothing comes out. Then, put olive tweezers, small and large, in the fire and blow on them until they become very hot.
Then take one, either small or large, depending on the wound and the place where the artery has ruptured. Place the hot instrument directly on the artery after quickly removing your finger, and hold it there until the bleeding stops.
If the blood gushes out when you lift your finger from the mouth of the artery and extinguishes the hot instrument, quickly take another one from the instruments in the prepared fire. Continue doing this, one after another, until the bleeding stops.
Be cautious not to burn a nerve that might be there, as it could cause another disability for the patient. Know that if blood is bleeding from an artery, it cannot be cut, especially if the artery is large, except by one of four methods: either by cauterization as we said, or by amputation if it has not already separated. For if it is amputated, its ends will contract and the blood flow will stop. Alternatively, it can be tightly tied with threads, or medicines that cause clotting can be applied and secured firmly with bandages.
And as for those who attempt to stop it with a ligature or by tightening with cloth or placing burning substances and the like, it will not be stopped at all except rarely. If any of that occurs to someone and there is no physician or medicine available, he should promptly place his index finger on the mouth of the wound itself as we have described.
And he should tighten it greatly until the blood is contained and flows over the wound and on the artery, and the finger should not be removed from it with very cold water continuously until the blood coagulates, thickens, and stops. During this time, you should look at what it needs of cauterization or medicine.
The Second Chapter.
On incisions, cauterization, bloodletting, surgeries, and the like.
Khalef said, we have mentioned in the first chapter every disease that can be treated with cauterization by fire and burning medicines, their causes, reasons, instruments, and forms of cautery devices. I have arranged this from head to foot in sections.
And I follow the same path in this chapter to make it easy for the student to understand what is required.
Before I begin, you should know, my children, that this chapter contains more risks than what is in the first chapter on cauterization.
For that reason, the warning should be more severe because the work in this chapter often involves bloodletting, which is essential for life, when opening a vein or incising a tumor, cauterizing an abscess, treating surgery, extracting an arrow, or incising a stone and other similar procedures that all carry risks and fear, and death often occurs in most of them.
And I advise you to avoid what is dubious for you, for various kinds of people with different ailments may come to you in this craft; some of them may be weary of their illness and have become indifferent to death.
Due to the severity of his illness and the length of his suffering, and with the disease settled in a way that indicates death; and there are those who spend their wealth on you and provide for you, hoping for health, but his illness is severe. Therefore, it should not be for you to assist anyone who comes to you with such a condition at all.
Let your caution be greater than your desire and eagerness, and do not proceed with anything unless you have certain knowledge that is valid to you regarding the praiseworthy outcome. Use in all treatment of your patients the precedence of knowledge and warning about what safety will lead to.
For in that you will find support in acquiring praise, glory, remembrance, and commendation. May God guide you to wisdom, O sons, and not deprive you of the right and success. Indeed, that is in His hand; there is no god but He.
I have arranged this chapter into sections following what was mentioned in the chapter on cauterization, from the ankle to the foot, to make it easier for you to find what you need from it, if God wills.
The first section.
On the treatment of water that accumulates in the heads of children.
This ailment often occurs in children at birth if the midwife presses the child's head without gentleness. It may also occur due to a hidden illness that is not known.
I have not seen this ailment except in children, and all that I saw of them quickly met death. Therefore, I deemed it best to refrain from treating it. Indeed, I saw a child whose head was filled with water, and the head grew larger each day. Until the child could not even sit up due to the enlargement of his head, and the moisture increased until he died.
This moisture either gathers between the skin and the bone or accumulates beneath the bone on the dura mater. The procedure for this is as follows: if the moisture is between the skin and the bone and the swelling is small, it should be cut in the middle of the head with one transverse incision, about two inches long, so that the moisture can flow out.
